s. List of AHRQ QIs that are endorsed measures by the National Quality Forum t. Summary of Quality Control Activities

C.8.2. Organize All Documentation The Contractor shall propose for the COR's approval and, once approved, shall implement a uniform series of products that address the documentation needs described above. For AHRQ QI software and measures, documentation shall not be recreated annually but instead be updated, reviewed and improved appropriately and efficiently annually. All documentation shall be delivered in electronic format accompanied by a memo describing contents and structure. Documentation must also be maintained in an AHRQ approved documentation system. C.8.3. Maintain Library of QI Processing Programs The Contractor shall maintain a library of QI programs, including production source code where applicable, that create the AHRQ QI SAS and Windows based software tools by including them in the AHRQ QI Documentation System (see Section C.8). This includes any code used to create executable files or analytic files which generate covariate tables, and other parameters needed to run the software. Some of these files may have been developed under different mechanisms but will be provided by AHRQ. Large volumes of statistical processing programs are used in the creation of the AHRQ QI software tools. The Contractor shall keep records and document software requirements analyses, software development, testing, code documentation, quality assurance and software change management as necessary. The Contractor shall also maintain version control, and naming conventions. The Contractor shall develop and deliver a memo with a description of a proposed file maintenance system of files related to analysis and programming efforts. After receiving approval from the COR, the Contractor shall put the maintenance system into place that allows for routine review and backup of all AHRQ QI files as appropriate. The Contractor shall ensure appropriate disposition of project files that become no longer needed as work proceeds throughout the contract period. The Contractor shall include documentation of which files need COR approval before destruction can take place, and shall seek and obtain such approval as appropriate.

C.8.4. Develop and Maintain Documentation System As noted above, large volumes of documentation are generated under the AHRQ QI program, much of which is updated annually. The Contractor shall develop and maintain an accessible online internal documentation system that tracks, stores, archives and allows easy
Page 45 of 174

Solicitation No. 14-233-SOL-00087 Support for AHRQ Quality Indicators IV

access to all documentation. This documentation system shall provide secure storage of all documentation and have the capacity to impose security permissions or restrictions on documents, as deemed necessary by the AHRQ COR. The Contractor shall track and maintain all project-related documentation for access by AHRQ project staff identified by the AHRQ COR. C.8.4.1. Maintain Project Management Records The Contractor shall maintain a consistent style, format and quality in all AHRQ QI reports, special analyses, and written materials. In most cases, final, written materials shall be delivered by 1) posting to the AHRQ QI documentation system, and 2) delivering hard copies. All final reports, memos, and documentation shall be delivered electronically and with non-bound original and 2 hard copies. C.8.4.2. Assure Documentation Quality The volume of documentation generated by the AHRQ QI project each year requires careful control. The Contractor shall create an AHRQ QI policy for handling documentation and management records. The policy shall include methods for quality control such as naming conventions, version control, storage, and destruction of information when it is no longer needed. All Contractor staff shall adhere to the policies developed under this task. C.8.5.Maintain Archive and Back-up System for All Documentation The Contractor shall develop and implement a reliable back-up system to prevent permanent, accidental loss of any AHRQ QI documentation files. The Contractor shall preserve the current collection of documentation to ensure adequate support for current users. Back-up shall be in media and formats readily accessible to the AHRQ QI COR. If necessary to keep back-up files in a format that is readily accessible, the Contractor shall convert to a newer application at least once during the period of this contract. With approval of the AHRQ QI COR, the Contractor may archive certain older files and place them in an alternative storage site.

C.9. PROVIDE TECHNICAL SUPPORT TO AHRQ QI USERS The Contractor shall provide technical support to users and potential users of the AHRQ QI measures, software tools, written reports, and software documentation and all other products developed for the AHRQ QI project. Technical support provides a bridge between the AHRQ QIs and its users and potential users. It is intended to respond to and meet users' needs for assistance with or technical advice on AHRQ QI measures and products. The objective of the assistance is to increase the usefulness and use of AHRQ QI measures and products. Technical support is provided to current users and prospective users of the AHRQ QIs, and to anyone interested in learning about the project, its measures and its products. Recipients of technical support include hospitals, payers, business coalitions, researchers, data organizations, AHRQ staff, Federal government, state and local government, media, universities, research organizations and many other constituent groups. Methods for providing technical support
Page 46 of 174

Solicitation No. 14-233-SOL-00087 Support for AHRQ Quality Indicators IV

include: 1) explanations and methods for using AHRQ QI measures, software tools, and documentation, and 2) identification/referral of relevant written AHRQ QI reports. Users of AHRQ QI measures, software tools and products include health services clinicians, researchers, health policy analysts, health care decision makers and other constituent groups. They have backgrounds in medicine, nursing, economics and other social sciences, public health, and other fields. They represent a variety of sectors, including academia, private industry, the media, and government. The Contractor shall ensure that staff providing technical support are able to work with these various constituents, understand their questions, problems, and demands, and be able to investigate and communicate solutions to them. C.9.1. Develop Staff and Infrastructure for User Technical Support Services C.9.1.1 Develop AHRQ QI Expertise The Contractor shall ensure that staff providing technical support have sufficient knowledge to communicate with AHRQ QI users and respond to questions about AHRQ QI measures and products within one month of the start date of the contract. Sufficient knowledge requires the ability to address inquiries with basic information about AHRQ QIs. The Contractor shall ensure technical support staff acquires a thorough knowledge by the third month of the contract, at which time contract staff shall have the ability to respond to complex inquiries. For assistance in learning about previous practices in providing Technical Support, the government shall provide to the Contractor existing technical support materials to use as prototypes in maintaining or developing their own apparatus and mechanisms. These materials include a log of user questions and answers from the past year to serve as a prototype of technical support inquiries and responses. The Contractor shall develop their AHRQ QI knowledge through additional focused efforts to learn about the project as well as thorough on-the-job learning. It is expected that the technical assistance staff shall gain knowledge and experience with AHRQ QI measures and tools and shall apply that knowledge to inform users and project development. Focused efforts to develop AHRQ QI knowledge include:      Becoming thoroughly familiar with the AHRQ QI Web site Review of key AHRQ QI reports and technical documentation Attending AHRQ QI presentations given by project staff Reviewing AHRQ QI presentations and training materials Discussions with AHRQ staff

Page 47 of 174

Solicitation No. 14-233-SOL-00087 Support for AHRQ Quality Indicators IV

C.9.1.2. Establish Systems to Respond to and Monitor Inquiries C.9.1.2.1. E-mail The Contractor shall support AHRQ in monitoring an AHRQ dedicated e-mail address for QI technical support. The Contractor shall provide the majority of technical assistance via e-mail and will ensure that all inquiries are acknowledged within a 24 hour period and resolved within two business days or sooner for simpler requests and four business days for complex inquiries. For questions submitted via e-mail that are more easily and efficiently answered in person-to-person conversation, the Contractor shall respond by telephone and document the response. The Contractor shall support the technical assistance e-mail address within 2 weeks of the start date of the contract. The technical support email is routed to an AHRQ server. AHRQ shall forward technical support e-mails to the Contractor automatically and in real-time. C.9.1.2.2. Routing Protocol The Contractor shall develop and maintain routing protocols for ensuring that technical assistance inquiries are routed to the appropriate contract staff. Routing protocols shall include criteria for inquiries from priority users (e.g., Congressional offices, Partners, Federal government agencies, the media, and strategic organizations) that require notification of AHRQ staff. The Contractor shall provide AHRQ with a list of key Contractor personnel proposed to staff the technical support inquiries by level of help required for an inquiry. The list shall briefly explain the staffers' relevant capabilities and their response roles. The technical support staff and routing protocol require AHRQ approval prior to implementation. The Contractor shall submit both to the COR for approval by the end of the second month of the contract, and shall revise and resubmit both when there are changes in personnel or routing procedures. C.9.1.2.3. Contractor Staffing Responsibilities The Contractor's senior research staff shall provide oversight and leadership to ensuring timeliness and accuracy of all technical support responses. Routine questions about AHRQ QIs shall be handled by mid-level technical support staff who have relevant technical backgrounds, and who are knowledgeable about AHRQ QI measures and tools. Sophisticated questions about AHRQ QIs (e.g., the appropriate use of AHRQ QIs, the advisability of using a particular AHRQ QI measure for provider-level public reporting, etc.) shall be referred to and handled by experienced mid-level and senior-level Technical Support staff with relevant technical and analytic backgrounds who have specialized AHRQ QI expertise. Questions from priority audiences and public users with high-profile work require consultation with the COR (or other designated AHRQ staff) prior to responding.

Page 48 of 174

Solicitation No. 14-233-SOL-00087 Support for AHRQ Quality Indicators IV

C.9.2. Provide Technical Support to AHRQ QI Users C.9.2.1. Provide Assistance to Public Users The Contractor shall receive, analyze, respond to and track technical assistance requests that come from the public. The requests shall come by e-mail and telephone, directly from the user, or routed through or referred from AHRQ staff. Based on past experience, the Contractor may expect technical assistance to include the following types of activities:         Guidance on using AHRQ QIs and directing users to technical documentation Guidance on selecting and obtaining an appropriate AHRQ QIs for specific purposes Guidance on using AHRQ QI software tools Help troubleshooting AHRQ QI software problems Investigating potential software errors and potential errors with documentation Guidance on navigating the AHRQ QI Web site http://www.quality indicators.ahrq.hhs.gov/ Help in interpreting output Answers to questions about appropriate use and reporting of AHRQ QIs

Technical assistance to public users shall not include the task of providing any actual programming services, study designs, complex analyses, or running, revising or customizing software tools. When appropriate, the Contractor shall redirect users to other resources. Depending on the needs of the user, this could include such sources as the National Quality Forum, Joint Commission, American Hospital Association, the Centers for Medicare and Medicaid, the American Hospital Association, and the National Center for Quality Assurance. The Contractor shall be familiar with these and other relevant quality measurement organizations. The total expected volume of technical assistance requests is approximately 1,200 in Year 1 (100 per month times 12 months), and is expected to increase by no more than 3 percent each option year. For purposes of estimating resources and costs, the Contractor shall assume a mix of 40% simple inquiries, requiring approximately 15 minutes of assistance each, and 60% complex inquiries (requiring approximately 1 hour of assistance each).

Page 49 of 174

Solicitation No. 14-233-SOL-00087 Support for AHRQ Quality Indicators IV

C.9.2.2. Provide Assistance on Special Requests from Priority Audiences The Contractor shall provide assistance in responding to special requests for AHRQ QI information from priority audiences, as directed by the COR. The audiences may include but is not limited to AHRQ staff from other programs, Congressional offices, Federal government agencies, the media, HCUP Partners, and prominent organizations. The Contractor shall alert the AHRQ QI team to such requests, request guidance if needed in designating these inquiries as high priorities, and respond quickly. The responses may require generation and explanation of special statistical tables and other aggregate data, and assistance with use of software tools. AHRQ staff may also be involved in the response. Offerors should anticipate that activities outlined in this task requires approximately two Contractor staff days per month, with about one-third for senior-level staff to oversee the analysis and the remainder for mid-level or junior programming, technical, and clerical support. C.9.3. Monitor Technical Support Services C.9.3.1. Log Technical Support Inquiries The Contractor shall log all technical support inquiries into a database or other electronic system for tracking purposes. The Contractor shall flag inquiries that require follow-up for impact analysis and those from priority audiences. The Contractor shall ensure that the database or tracking system shall include at a minimum, but not limited to, the following types of information on each technical assistance request: date of request, date the assistance was provided, the organization, contact information, AHRQ QI product, a summary of the request including the reason the requestor needs the information or assistance, and a description of the information or assistance provided. This information is considered identifiable and is therefore subject to all relative privacy policies under the Paperwork Reduction Act of 1995. The database or tracking system shall have the capability of being sorted by organization name and date and the capability of searching on key words (for topics on which assistance was provided). The Contractor shall enter outcomes of the follow-up in the user database. The Contractor shall update the tracking system within three working days of the completion of a technical assistance request performed under task C.9 or receipt of a technical assistance description from AHRQ. C.9.3.2. Monitor Potential Impact from Technical Support Assistance The Contractor, as directed by the COR, shall follow-up on technical assistance provided to users with high-profile, high-impact, or resource-intensive work at selected appropriate time intervals to determine the outcome of the information provided to them, to ascertain any use and impact AHRQ QIs had, such as, used for decision making purposes, presentations in published reports or articles, or effect on policy, etc. The Contractor shall flag information on the use and impact the AHRQ QIs had, if any, for follow up in the user database or for potential development of an Impact Story.

Page 50 of 174

Solicitation No. 14-233-SOL-00087 Support for AHRQ Quality Indicators IV

C.9.3.3. Develop Standardized Responses and Limited Statistics The Contractor shall develop a set of standardized "best responses" for use in responding to routine technical assistance inquiries, and shall update these responses on a regular basis as improvements and variations to the response become apparent. The Contractor shall develop a limited number of tables with frequently requested AHRQ QI rates or cross-tabulations to facilitate responses for this information. C.9.4. Improve the Usefulness and Value of AHRQ QI Tools through User Feedback Contact with users during the course of providing technical support not only helps the user, but can also yield important information that could benefit the AHRQ QI project. In the course of providing assistance to knowledgeable AHRQ QI users, the Contractor shall elicit and document their suggestions for improvement of or enhancement of AHRQ QI data, tools, reports and technical support. Such feedback may include, but is not limited to, ideas for bettering existing AHRQ QI products, developing new products in the future, improving the dissemination of AHRQ QI information, and targeting special groups who would benefit from knowing more about AHRQ QIs. Possible improvements to providing technical support to users may include clarifying materials posted on the AHRQ QI Web site (www.qualityindicators.ahrq.gov), recommending new tools or instructions to help users, or developing user groups to share ideas. The Contractor shall document user suggestions, analyze them and communicate them to the COR. User suggestions shall be logged in the user database described in Section C.9.5. The suggestions shall be flagged and provided as technical support feedback in the quarterly Technical Support and Outreach Statistics Report to AHRQ described in Section C.9. C.9.5.MaintainaUserDatabase The Contractor shall develop and maintain an electronic database with information on user inquiries and technical support provided and usage of AHRQ QI. Maintaining a user database of information has four major purposes: 1. Document usage of technical support and AHRQ QI products in order to provide statistics on current Technical Support activities and AHRQ QI product use for future planning and development decisions for the project. The tracking shall also help fulfill required AHRQ reporting needs. 2. Document user suggestions and assessments of how the AHRQ QI project could be improved. 3. Follow up with select organizations to assess the value and impact of AHRQ QI products.

Page 51 of 174

Solicitation No. 14-233-SOL-00087 Support for AHRQ Quality Indicators IV

4. Track impacts from AHRQ QI use, such as reports published using AHRQ QIs, and policies developed as a result of using AHRQ QI products. The information to be kept in the database includes user email (as allowed by Government privacy regulations), user affiliation (university, government agency, research organization, etc.), AHRQ QI product (identify the software tool, report, etc.), issue addressed, method of contact, level of response effort, and when obtainable, the purpose of their use of AHRQ QIs and any resultant outcomes or actions that result from it. This information is considered identifiable and is therefore subject to all relative privacy policies under the Paperwork Reduction Act of 1995. The Contractor shall flag technical assistance requests that were resource-intensive. The Contractor shall flag inquiries for special requests from priority audiences and from public users who have high-profile or high-impact work. These entries shall be followed up, with outcomes entered in the user database (see Section C.9.5) The Contractor shall maintain records for the maximum time allowed by Government record keeping requirements. The Contractor shall maintain de-identified information for the duration of the contract, for use in look backs and trend analyses. The Contractor shall maintain the database to serve also as the source for information and statistics to be generated quarterly in Technical Support and Outreach Statistics Reports and other special reports for management purposes (Described in Section C.9.6). The information in the user database shall be set up so that information can be sorted by user's organization, date, AHRQ QI product category, assistance provided, outcome, and other important variables. The system shall have the capability of being searched by keywords. The user database shall be kept up-to-date, with information entered promptly to allow tracking the completion of technical assistance requests. C.9.6. Provide Technical Support and Outreach Reports The Contractor shall aggregate and summarize all information derived from the database on users and uses of AHRQ QI products (see Section C.9.5), into quarterly Technical Support and Outreach Statistics Reports. The Contractor shall provide the internal reports to the COR quarterly per calendar year for management purposes. The reports shall provide counts of user contacts by user affiliation, AHRQ QI product that help is needed for, level of difficulty of inquiry, and method of contact, and other items deemed important by AHRQ or the Contractor. The counts are to be provided for each quarter in the calendar year and from one year earlier. The Contractor shall ensure the reports also capture all outreach activities, presentations given, training sessions held, and booths staffed for all events that took place in the previous quarter. The report shall provide an explanation of the activity, a description of the content, audience, attendance summary, results, and any issues raised or suggestions for improvements to the AHRQ QI products, and an opinion as to whether this activity, conference, meeting or session shall be supported with a similar activity, presentation or AHRQ QI presence in the future. The reports shall include information on the outcome and impact of the activity when

known. The Contractor shall also aggregate and include this information in summary form in an Annual Report of AHRQ QI Outreach Activities. C.10. PROVIDE TECHNICAL SUPPORT TO AHRQ & DHHS MEASUREMENT INITIATIVES Over the course of the contract, HHS, AHRQ and/or its contracting staff will require periodic technical support, documentation and software to facilitate or support their work related to the AHRQ QIs. Offerors should anticipate that these activities shall involve a total of one contractor FTEs. C.10.1. National Quality Measures Clearinghouse (NQMC) The Contractor shall provide technical support to complete the annual NQMC update and verification process for the AHRQ QIs. Specifically, the Contractor shall:

Page 53 of 174

Solicitation No. 14-233-SOL-00087 Support for AHRQ Quality Indicators IV

-

Work with the NQMC regarding the update process and schedule. Notify NQMC when changes are made to the AHRQ QI measures. Review the measure summary developed for each AHRQ QI measure for accuracy and completeness prior to posting to the NQMC Web site. Confirm currency of published AHRQ QI measure summaries on an annual basis.

For the purposes of scheduling, the Contractor shall assume that the NQMC updates will occur in May of the calendar year. C.10.2. National Healthcare Quality Report (NHQR) & National Healthcare Disparities Report (NHDR) Each year, as part of the production of the NHQR and NHDR, AHRQ applies the AHRQ QI software to the HCUP NIS, SID, NEDS and SEDD datasets, and a special analytic file that supports national QI estimates by race/ethnicity for the NHDR. The main products include consistently defined QI estimates in tables, documentation of methods, special analyses, and coordination with HCUP Partners. The latter effort aims to support States in use of the Reports and seeking to obtain their permission to publish State-level estimates for the QIs in the Reports. The Contractor shall support the production of the AHRQ QI rates in the reports, by responding to technical questions, providing specialized risk adjustment tables with separate coefficients for age and gender breakouts, adapt AHRQ QI SAS programs that allow calculation of stratified rates by age and gender, and formally brief AHRQ staff working on the NHQR and NHDR at least annually on upcoming enhancements and updates to the measures and tools. The Contractor shall also provide technical support on the application and interpretation of the AHRQ QIs as directed by the COR. Previous reports and documentation of methodology can be found at http://www.ahrq.gov/research/findings/nhqrdr/index.html, and http://www.hcupus.ahrq.gov/reports/methods/2012_03.pdf for the 2012 NHQR and NHDR. For the purposes of scheduling for the proposal, Offerors should assume that all required software and documentation materials will be delivered in March of the calendar year. C.10.3. HCUP Partners The AHRQ QI project relies heavily on the databases and supplemental files created and supported under the HCUP partnership. Data organizations voluntarily participate in HCUP by allowing the inclusion of their data and by participating in project initiatives, including the AHRQ QIs. As such, the AHRQ QI project is committed to supporting the HCUP Partners in their use of the AHRQ QIs. HCUP Partners are generally interested in receiving additional guidance and technical assistance on the application and uses of the AHRQ QIs. In the past, HCUP Partners have requested AHRQ to facilitate communication and information exchange among Partners about using the AHRQ QIs in public reporting and quality improvement initiatives. Such support provided by the AHRQ QI project ultimately improves the quality, consistency and usefulness of the AHRQ QI measures and tools. The purpose of this task is to provide technical support for HCUP Partners to facilitate their use of the AHRQ QI measures and tools in their own state specific quality improvement and public reporting initiatives. The

Page 54 of 174

Solicitation No. 14-233-SOL-00087 Support for AHRQ Quality Indicators IV

lead of this task shall serve as the HCUP liaison for the QI project. The Contractor shall ensure this liaison is aware and able to help resolve all inquiries submitted by the HCUP partners. The Contractor shall perform the tasks specified below to provide AHRQ QI technical support to Partners. The Contractor shall participate in quarterly conference calls with AHRQ staff on this task and provide a quarterly report to AHRQ summarizing task activities. The report shall include brief descriptions of workgroup calls, LISTSERV activity, brief descriptions of conferences, brief descriptions of Federal and national initiatives, postings on the website, individualized technical assistance to Partners, etc. as it relates to HCUP Partners.

C.10.3.1. Provide Technical Assistance to HCUP Partners Consistent with the standard procedures established under the technical assistance task, all HCUP Partners shall receive timely technical assistance (within 24 hours). The Contractor shall notify the COR immediately of any HCUP Partner queries, the issue in question, the solution and the time frame for implementing that solution. The Contractor shall copy the COR on all email correspondence with HCUP Partners and notify in writing of all telephone conversations. The Contractor shall ensure that the COR participates in the telephone conversations, unless the COR indicates otherwise. C.10.3.2. Conduct HCUP Partner Workgroup The Contractor shall support an AHRQ workgroup of representatives from HCUP Partner organizations when the need arises, as directed by the COR. The workgroup may be on specific measurement topic areas of interest to Partners or AHRQ or they may be focused on specific issues related to the AHRQ QI software. The Contractor shall handle all the logistical arrangements for the conference calls, such as notification of meeting time, agenda, conference call phone line, and minutes of the calls. The Contractor shall anticipate one active workgroup with three calls per year. The size of the workgroup shall vary depending on the nature of the workgroup objective and Partner interest. The Contractor shall develop summaries of the calls and make them available electronically to the participants and ready for posting on HCUP-US, at the discretion of the COR. C.10.4. My Own Network, Powered by AHRQ (MONAHRQŽ) The Contractor shall support the MONAHRQ project in the following ways:  Support the creation of new MONAHRQ software packages that incorporate AHRQ QIs as needed. Provide documentation and/or technical assistance to help MONAHRQ developers understand and work with AHRQ QIs and software, as needed. Such documentation or assistance is particularly important when new features or major new updates to the QIs occur. Although the MONAHRQ project provides its own technical support, some assistance may be required to help MONAHRQ Technical Assistance (TA) respond to user requests that deal with the Quality Indicators or Windows QI software specifically.

Page 55 of 174

Solicitation No. 14-233-SOL-00087 Support for AHRQ Quality Indicators IV



Because MONAHRQ incorporates the AHRQ QIs, the Contractor shall communicate and coordinate with MONAHRQ developers when planning updates to the QI software. These updates may affect how the AHRQ QI software interacts with or is used by MONAHRQ. Examples include changes to the QI technical specification that change the meaning, labels or range of rates, QI software's internal database structure, data load process, user interface, and the interface between the AHRQ QI WinQI with the MONAHRQ user interface. More significant examples of software updates include adding new measures or introducing new features such as time trend analysis or stratification options. Where relevant, the Contractor shall ensure that changes to the QI software are planned such that they can be incorporated in MONAHRQ in a timely and efficient manner. In coordination with MONAHRQ developers, implement changes to the QI software that directly support the MONAHRQ project. A modest example is enabling the QI software to output measure results in a specific format needed by MONAHRQ. A more significant example is restructuring the Windows QI software so as to make the MONAHRQ build process more efficient and error free.



The Contractor shall participate in conference calls with MONAHRQ software development and management staff, as needed (Offerors may assume 6 times per year). C.10.5. C.11. Support Technical Dissemination, Communications and Education

C.11.1. Maintain Content on the AHRQ QI Web Site AHRQ currently maintains the AHRQ QI Web site on an AHRQ server. In general, the Contractor shall coordinate with AHRQ staff to post new/updated content to the AHRQ QI Web site with prior approval from the COR. Conversion of documents into HTML shall also require review and approval from AHRQ. C.11.1.1. Maintain and Update Technical Assistance Web Pages The Contractor shall create and construct new web pages on the AHRQ QI Web site to communicate relevant and accurate technical assistance information for users. These pages, which shall be for public access, shall provide guidance on the types of Technical Support provided and not provided, expected response time, how to locate technical documentation, and other helpful information. Technical assistance web pages shall include a section with frequently asked questions and/or an index, and a search capability. The Contractor shall provide the COR with recommendations on content and format for new technical assistance web pages, and suggestions for improving existing Web pages. With the COR's approval, the Contractor shall provide the new content to the AHRQ QI web site manager who will implement Web site changes with the COR's approval. The Contractor shall support the AHRQ QI web site manager to maintain and update the technical assistance web pages as needed for provision of accurate information to the public. Web page development shall be delivered in a format compatible with the AHRQ Web site, and adhere to Federal government and DHHS standards, including Section 508 of the American Disability Act. Technical assistance web pages shall be coordinated with the Technical Support activities described in Section C.15. C.11.1.2. Ensure Web Pages Adhere to Federal Web Site Policy and Regulations The Contractor shall be familiar with law, regulations and policies for Federal Web sites as made available on the FirstGov Web site at http://www.firstgov.gov/webcontent/laws_regs_policies.shtml. Federal guidelines require that Web site design and maintenance give careful consideration to public accessibility needs, although standards and best practices for accessibility are expected to emerge and evolve over time.
Page 58 of 174

Solicitation No. 14-233-SOL-00087 Support for AHRQ Quality Indicators IV

Web pages and documents created under this effort shall be in compliance with Section 508. If existing content is found to be not compliant, the Contractor shall re-format such documents to ensure compliance with section 508 of the American Disabilities Act and provide them to the AHRQ QI web site manager. C.11.1.3. Adhere to AHRQ WEB PRODUCT AND WEB SITE DEVELOPMENT GUIDELINES The following section highlights basic issues that need to be addressed when developing Web pages, tools or sites under contract that will be publicly available when launched to ensure deliverables are on target, in compliance with legal and policy requirements, and do not require expensive rework to meet Federal and Department of Health and Human Services requirements for information resources. Retrofitting Web-based products after the fact is highly undesirable because it adds time and costs to the process of making these products publicly available. The Contractor shall ensure that all products that are developed with the intent of being posted on the AHRQ Web site meet the minimum requirements noted below. The Contractor shall note that since the website is being hosted on an AHRQ server, some of these requirements may not be applicable. The Contractor is expected to adhere to all applicable requirements. C.11.1.3.1. Titles of Products Coordinate with your COR on the titles of your products. They need to be concise and relevant to the purpose of the project, but cannot include the name of the contractor or grantee as the performing organization as part of the title. Report titles should be no more than 10-words maximum and Web-based tools should be no more than 5-words maximum (make every word count--eliminate initial articles such as "The" or "A" ). Titles need to be distinct enough to differentiate among similar sounding products. C.11.1.3.2. Quality Control/Editorial Review This involves checking for spelling and grammar mistakes, formatting issues, general consistency, and style. This should be done by the AHRQ contractor prior to submission of the final product for posting on the AHRQ Web site. Federal resources follow the GPO Style Manual which is available electronically at: http://www.gpoaccess.gov/stylemanual/2008.html . C.11.1.3.3. Accessibility As an agency of the Federal Government, AHRQ must ensure that anything that is posted on our Web site is in compliance with requirements for information resources under Section 508 of the Rehabilitation Act. Also, federally funded resources need to be generally available to users in multiple formats to ensure that we are not forcing a particular platform, operational system, or proprietary software package on users.

Page 59 of 174

Solicitation No. 14-233-SOL-00087 Support for AHRQ Quality Indicators IV

C.11.1.3.4. Intellectual Property Rights Before we can post a product on the AHRQ Web site, we must have a written explanation (which the Contractor shall provide) of the following four questions:     Who retains the copyright? Who has licenses for what purposes and uses? What are the constraints imposed? Who grants permission for further use or adoption?

C.11.1.3.5. Editorial Review All content for upload needs to be reviewed to ensure consistency and compliance with best practices and established style and conventions. As a minimum, the copy needs to be production edited to ensure there are no typos and the GPO Style Manual is followed for punctuation, spelling, use of numerals, abbreviations, etc. Do not use unexplained acronyms; they need to be spelled out on first reference in any document or file. There should not be anything marked DRAFT on a public site. Once the materials are uploaded, they are published and considered in the "public domain." Do not use placeholders for content that does not exist. Government funded sites should not have anything designated "under construction." A process needs to be established for regular review of content and updating. Additional materials need to undergo editorial review and be approved before uploading. The GPO Style Guide is available electronically as a reference at: http://www.gpoaccess.gov/stylemanual/browse.html C.11.1.3.6. Accessibility Under the Rehabilitation Act, Federal agencies have an obligation to provide equal access for the disabled to their information and services. Requirements are specified in section 504 for individual accommodation and more recently in section 508 for electronic and information technology, which includes Web sites and multimedia products. Equivalent alternatives are required for auditory and visual information, such as providing alternative descriptive text for images for the blind and providing captions for audio-video files for the deaf. Written transcripts are required for all streaming audio. PDF files can be offered in conjunction with accessible files, such as HTML versions, but avoid uploading PDF-only versions of documents unless they are fully accessible PDF formats. AHRQ has software used to evaluate Web sites and can provide a report on any accessibility violations that would need to be addressed before launch. Specific requirements are available at: http://www.section508.gov C.11.1.3.7. Privacy A privacy policy notice must be prominently displayed, and the Web site host has to follow it. A machine-readable format (P3P) of the privacy policy notice must also be uploaded to the site. A Privacy Impact Assessment is conducted to determine what kind of personal information
Page 60 of 174

Solicitation No. 14-233-SOL-00087 Support for AHRQ Quality Indicators IV

is contained within a system, what is done with that information, and how that information is protected. Sites are periodically audited to ensure that they observe their stated privacy policy. A Privacy Act System notice may need to be prepared and published for users to register on a site if the registrations represent a group of records, under the control of the Agency (or a contractor), that can be retrieved by personal identifier. This notice must go through several levels of review-including the Office of General Counsel--and be published in the Federal Register. Persistent cookies cannot be used on Federal sites unless the Secretary of HHS grants an exemption, and this involves a strong justification and review process. C.11.1.3.8. Web Site Mailbox Every Web site must provide full contact information for AHRQ and have a Contact Us link for submission of comments or questions as a customer feedback mechanism. Web site e-mail is subject to the same privacy and records management issues that affect the overall Web site as well as departmental standards for handling inquiries and customer feedback. Each Web site must provide relevant Frequently Asked Questions that are included in the customer relationship management system used to handle AHRQ Web site inquiries. C.11.1.3.9. Records Management All content on the site and e-mail generated by the site must be archived electronically and handled according to records retention schedules and disposition authorities as established with the National Archives and Record Administration. This requirement also affects Web site log files and statistical reporting on Web site usage. For guidance on requirements, go to: http://www.archives.gov/records-mgmt/policy/managing-web-records-index.html C.11.1.3.10. Information Collection Budget If a Web site is used to collect information from users, such as for surveys, evaluations, or beta testing feedback, then the Office of Management and Budget must first approve the burden hours for such an effort for this collection. A notice must be posted on the Web site at the point of collection with the OMB approval number and a statement on the process of collection. C.11.1.3.11. Intellectual Property Copyright and trademark protections need to be observed on Web sites. Permissions for use must be granted for any copyrighted information included and registered trademarks need to be reflected in copy. Any copyright or trademark constraints related to materials uploaded to a site must be specified for users. Public domain does not extend outside the borders of the United States. Therefore, foreign countries must request specific permission for use. Given the global nature of the Internet, citation as to source is a critical issue.

C.11.2 Coordinate, Support and Implement Educational Activities Education and transparency of AHRQ QI methodology and program-specific processes is an important requirement of this initiative. Over the last several years, the AHRQ QIs have become a cornerstone of the Agency's agenda for measuring and improving the quality of health care. As noted earlier, the AHRQ QIs have increasingly been used by policymakers, insurers, and hospital administrators for public reporting, pay for performance, and quality improvement efforts. As a result, stakeholders are extremely interested in knowing what AHRQ is doing with respect to the development, maintenance, and enhancement of the AHRQ QIs. The Contractor shall support AHRQ in its effort to engage its users and key stakeholders in activities supporting education and transparency of its AHRQ QI measures, methodology and tools. Examples of activities for which the Contractor shall provide support include, but are not limited to:   Conducting informational webinars for multiple audiences Establishing mechanism and process for disseminating information (via different media) about: a. New quality indicator updates and activities o History of the AHRQ QI program and evolution of the AHRQ QIs o List of AHRQ QIs that are in development o List of NQF endorsed AHRQ QI measures o How indicators are developed o How individuals are chosen to be on clinical panel reviews o Partnerships with other measurement programs that are new or ongoing o Uses of QIs in quality improvement, public reporting and pay for performance initiatives

C.11.2.1. Develop and Deliver In-Person Expository and Training Presentations Each year, the Contractor shall develop and deliver 2 presentations per year at conferences, meetings and other venues, to educate a variety of audiences (health service researchers, policy analysts, decision makers, social scientists, clinicians, etc.) about AHRQ QI measures and tools, its applications and the benefits of its use, and to teach select audiences how to actually use AHRQ QI software tools. The expository presentations shall range from basic overviews to advanced explanations of the AHRQ QI project, using 45-minute, 60-minute, 90-minute, and all day PowerPoint slide shows. In the past, presentations have been made at Academy Health,

C.12. PROVIDE DATA CATALOG, CONFIDENTIALITY AND SECURITY PROTECTIONS The Contractor shall protect the security and confidentiality of HCUP databases, Medicare databases, Medicaid databases project files, and any individually identifiable information obtained and used in the project. The Contractor shall develop procedures and mechanisms that shall adhere to all Federal, DHHS, and AHRQ IT security and confidentiality regulations. The Contractor shall also take other steps that are deemed necessary by the COR to adequately protect data confidentiality. The Contractor shall keep a detailed log of all staff who have completed the data security and privacy requirements. C.12.1. Adhere to HCUP Confidentiality and Security Provisions HCUP data are routinely used to update and test the AHRQ QI specifications and tools. Due to the nature of the HCUP data and the data partnerships, specific, stringent data security and usage rules are in place for any HCUP data user. As a major user of this resource, the Contractor must adhere to all such HCUP confidentiality and security provisions. The AHRQ HCUP project team will provide electronic training, data use agreements, and guidance on data protections. A data security plan shall be provided to the AHRQ HCUP COR as part of the data security requirements as described below in C.12.2. The identities of patients and physicians who might be included in the HCUP databases are protected from disclosure by the statutes that govern the activities of AHRQ. Additionally, AHRQ excludes identities of patients and physicians from
Page 64 of 174

Solicitation No. 14-233-SOL-00087 Support for AHRQ Quality Indicators IV

publicly released HCUP databases and the HCUP Data Use Agreements (DUA) prohibit users from making any effort to determine the identity of any person contained in publicly released databases (including but not limited to patients, physicians, and other health care providers). The identity of institutions (e.g., hospitals) included in the HCUP databases are protected from disclosure, according to the laws of the state providing the information, or according to HCUP agreements between the data organization and AHRQ. Permission is obtained from some of the HCUP Partner data organizations to include hospital identification on restricted access public release databases. When such information appears in HCUP databases, it may be used only for the purpose of conducting research, which includes linking institutional information from outside data sets to enhance analysis and aggregate statistical reporting. Additionally, HCUP DUAs preclude using information about individual establishments in the HCUP databases for commercial or competitive purposes involving those establishments, or to determine the rights, benefits, or privileges of those establishments. Users of the data must not identify establishments directly or by inference in disseminated material. The Contractor shall designate a Data Security Officer who is responsible for the oversight and use of sensitive data, like HCUP and other similar databases. The Data Security Officer shall be familiar with the existing confidentiality statutes and regulations governing HHS, AHRQ and contractors to AHRQ. These include but may not be limited to: 1) the Privacy Act of 1974 and the Public Health Service Act (42 U.S.C. 299c-3(c)); 2) the Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act; 3) Title 13, Subtitle D of the American Recovery and Reinvestment Act of 2009; 4) AHRQ Information Security and Privacy Policy and DHHS regulations; and 5) HCUP DUAs required of staff and contractors, and MOAs and DUAs in place with Partner data organizations. In some cases, a participating data organization may require a specific security or confidentiality protection. C.12.2. AHRQ and HHS Security and Privacy Requirements C.12.2.1. AHRQ and HHS Security and Privacy Requirements C.12.2.1.1. Adherence to security and privacy policy. The Contractor shall comply with all Federal and Department of Health and Human Services (HHS) security and privacy guidelines in effect at the time of the award of this contract. A list of applicable United States (U.S.) laws, Office of Management and Budget (OMB) requirements, HHS policies, standards and guidance, and Federal Government Computer Security guidelines can be located on the Secure One HHS website. The Contractor shall perform periodic reviews to ensure compliance with all information security and privacy requirements. The Contractor shall make all system information and documentation produced in support of the Contract available to the agency and agency auditors upon request. See Appendix 4 for list of references.

Page 65 of 174

Solicitation No. 14-233-SOL-00087 Support for AHRQ Quality Indicators IV

C.12.2.1.2. Perimeter defense and notification. The Contractor shall ensure that the system and the information it contains are secured using appropriate perimeter defense technologies and that these technologies are monitored for anomalous traffic behavior. The Contractor shall immediately report any unauthorized system access to the agency COR and/or System Owner. C.12.2.1.3. Protection of sensitive information. The Contractor shall ensure that sensitive information is protected by information security and privacy controls commensurate with the risk associated with the potential loss or compromise of this information. For purposes of this contract, information is sensitive if the loss of confidentiality or integrity could be expected to have a serious, severe or catastrophic adverse effect on organizational operations, organizational assets, or individuals (FIPS, 2004). Further, the loss of sensitive information confidentiality or integrity could: (i) cause a significant or severe degradation in mission capability to an extent and duration that the organization is unable to perform its primary functions or the effectiveness of the functions is significantly reduced; (ii) result in significant or major damage to organizational assets; (iii) result in significant or major financial loss; or (iv) result in significant, severe or catastrophic harm to individuals. Personally identifiable information (PII) is a subset of sensitive information and is defined as data which can potentially be used to identify, locate, or contact an individual, or potentially reveal the activities, characteristics, or other details about a person. PII shall receive a level of protection commensurate with the risk associated with the loss or compromise of sensitive information. C.12.2.1.4. Sensitive information on public systems. The Contractor shall ensure that sensitive information is not stored, processed or transmitted on a publicly-available system (via the Internet) without the appropriate controls in place and specific authorization from the AHRQ Chief Information Officer (CIO). C.12.2.1.5. Privacy requirements. The Contractor shall conduct and maintain a Privacy Impact Assessment (PIA) as defined by Section 208 of the E-Government Act of 2002 and Federal Acquisition Regulation (FAR) Clause 52-239-1, and required by HHS policy. The PIA shall be completed in accordance with HHS PIA guidance (http://www.hhs.gov/ocio/securityprivacy/privacyresources/pias.html) . Periodic reviews shall be conducted to determine if a major change to the system has occurred, and if a PIA update is subsequently required. If it is determined that an update is necessary, the Contractor shall make the necessary changes to the PIA. The Contractor shall abide by all requirements of the Privacy Act of 1974 and FAR Clause 52-239-1. Pursuant to those requirements, the Contractor shall create and publish a System of Records Notice (SORN) in the Federal Register when required and shall publish an updated SORN following a major change to the system, as directed by OMB Memorandum (M) 03-22,

Page 66 of 174

Solicitation No. 14-233-SOL-00087 Support for AHRQ Quality Indicators IV

OMB Guidance for Implementing the Privacy Provisions of the E-Government Act of 2002, or subsequent replacement guidance. C.12.2.1.6. System accreditation. The Contractor shall certify and accredit all systems in conformance with the standards set forth by the Federal Information Security Management Act (FISMA) and National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) Special Publication (SP) 800-37, Guide for the Security Certification and Accreditation of Federal Information Systems, prior to the system becoming operational. This activity shall be performed in conjunction with the initial development of the system, updated when a major change occurs to the system, and renewed no less than every three years. All system certification and accreditation (C&A) packages shall be compliant with all Public Law (PL)-107-347, OMB mandates, FIPS, and additional applicable NIST guidance. This guidance includes, but is not limited to FIPS 199, FIPS 200, NIST SP 800-18, NIST SP 800-30, NIST SP 800-37, NIST SP 800-53, NIST SP 800-53A, and NIST SP 800-60. All NIST and FIPS documentation can be found at the NIST website (http://csrc.nist.gov/). HHS has created a C&A checklist to facilitate compliance with the OMB-mandated C&A process. The HHS C&A Checklist will be provided upon contract initiation. Prior to becoming operational, all systems must receive a signed Authorization to Operate (ATO) issued by the agency Designated Authorization Authority (DAA). No system will be permitted into the production environment without a valid, signed ATO. C.12.2.1.7. Annual requirements. The Contractor shall be responsible for meeting ongoing information security and privacy system requirements. These include, but are not limited to, performing annual system testing, completing an annual system self-assessment, and supporting quarterly and annual AHRQ FISMA reporting. Additionally, AHRQ reserves the right to test or review the system security and privacy controls at any time. C.12.2.1.8. Security and privacy training. All Contractors shall receive general awareness training and role-based training, commensurate with the responsibilities required to perform the work articulated in the terms and conditions of the Contract. The Contractor shall be responsible for ensuring each contractor employee has completed the AHRQ Security Awareness Training as required by the agency prior to performing any contract work or accessing any system, and on an annual basis thereafter, throughout the period of performance of the contract. The Contractor shall maintain a list of all individuals who have completed this training and shall submit this list to the COR upon request. As a part of this training, the Contractor shall ensure that all staff read, agree to, and sign the HHS Rules of Behavior (http://www.hhs.gov/ocio/policy/hhs-ocio-20100002.001s_hhs_rules_of_behavior.html ).

Page 67 of 174

Solicitation No. 14-233-SOL-00087 Support for AHRQ Quality Indicators IV

The Contractor shall ensure that all contractors with significant security responsibilities, as defined by HHS, receive commensurate role-based training. As stated in the Secure One HHS Memorandum, Role-Based Training (RBT) of Personnel with Significant Security Responsibilities, significant security responsibilities are defined as the responsibilities associated with a given role or position, which, upon execution, could have the potential to adversely impact the security posture of one or more HHS systems. The Contractor shall maintain a list of all individuals that possess significant security responsibilities and the subsequent role-based training courses completed, and shall submit this list to the COR upon request. C.12.2.1.9. Electronic communication. All Contractor staff that have access to and use of HHS electronic mail (e-mail) must identify themselves as contractors on all outgoing e-mail messages, including those sent in reply or forwarded to another user. The Contractor shall ensure all contractor staff embed an e-mail signature ("AutoSignature") or an electronic business card ("V-card") within each electronic correspondence to automatically display "Contractor" in the signature. C.12.2.1.10. Clearances. The Contractor shall ensure all staff have the required level of security clearance commensurate with the sensitivity of the information being stored, processed, transmitted or otherwise handled by the System or required to perform the work stipulated by the contract. At the minimum, all Contractor staff shall be subjected to a Public Trust background check and be granted a Public Trust clearance before access to the System or other HHS resources is granted. C.12.2.1.11. Non-Disclosure. The Contractor shall not release, publish, or disclose agency information to unauthorized personnel, and shall protect such information in accordance with the provisions of the following laws and any other pertinent laws and regulations governing the confidentiality of sensitive information: -18 U.S.C. 641 (Criminal Code: Public Money, Property or Records) -18 U.S.C. 1905 (Criminal Code: Disclosure of Confidential Information) - PL 96-511 (Paperwork Reduction Act) The Contractor shall ensure that each contractor employee who may have access to agency information under this contract shall complete and sign the Commitment to Protect Non-Public Information - Contractor Agreement (Non-Disclosure Agreement). A copy of each signed and witnessed Non-Disclosure Agreement shall be submitted to the COR prior to performing any work under the contract. C.12.2.1.12. MOBILE DEVICE ENCRYPTION. The Contractor shall: (a) encrypt all laptop computers, mobile devices and portable media which store or process, or may store or process, sensitive information using FIPS 140-2
Page 68 of 174

Solicitation No. 14-233-SOL-00087 Support for AHRQ Quality Indicators IV

compliant encryption technology; (b) verify that encryption products have been validated under the Cryptographic Module Validation Program (http://csrc.nist.gov/groups/STM/index.html) to confirm compliance with FIPS 140-2; (c) establish key recovery mechanisms to ensure the ability to decrypt and recover sensitive information by authorized personnel; and (d) generate and manage encryption keys securely to prevent unauthorized decryption of information. For more information, reference the HHS Encryption Standard for Mobile Devices and Portable Media (http://www.hhs.gov/ocio/policy/20080007001s.html ). C.12.2.1.13. DESKTOP ENCRYPTION. The Contractor shall: (a) encrypt all desktop computers which store or process, or may store or process, sensitive information using FIPS 140-2 compliant encryption technology; (b) verify that encryption products have been validated under the Cryptographic Module Validation Program (http://csrc.nist.gov/groups/STM/index.html) to confirm compliance with FIPS 140-2; (c) establish key recovery mechanisms to ensure the ability to decrypt and recover sensitive information by authorized personnel; and (d) generate and manage encryption keys securely to prevent unauthorized decryption of information. In the case that appropriate compensating controls are implemented to protect sensitive desktop computers, the requirement for encryption may be waived with approval from the AHRQ Chief Information Security Officer (CISO). For more information, reference the HHS Encryption Standard for Mobile Devices and Portable Media (http://www.hhs.gov/ocio/policy/20080007001s.html). C.12.2.1.14. MINIMUM SECURITY CONFIGURATIONS. The Contractor shall certify applications are fully functional, operate as intended, and comply with the HHS Minimum Security Configurations for Operating Systems (currently HHS has minimum configuration standards for Windows 2000 Server, Windows 2000 Professional, Windows 2003 Server, Windows NT, Windows 7, Solaris, HP-UX, Redhat Linux, Oracle, and Cisco IOS). These standard security configurations shall be provided to the Contractor at the time of contract initiation and upon completion of the required Non-Disclosure Agreements. Additionally, the Contractor shall adhere to these configurations when developing the system. As standard configurations may change frequently, the Contractor must ensure applications remain compliant with the most recent set of security configurations. Additionally, for desktops and laptops within the system boundary, the Contractor shall comply with the configurations defined in the HHS Federal Desktop Core Configuration (FDCC) standards, which were designed to meet the requirements mandated by OMB. The FDCC standards will be provided upon contract initiation. The installation, operation, maintenance, updates, and/or patching of software shall not alter the approved HHS Minimum Security Configurations or the HHS FDCC standards. Applications designed for normal end users shall run in the standard user context without elevated system administration privileges. Exceptions to the HHS requirements must be documented, accompanied by compensating controls, and approved by the HHS CISO and the AHRQ CISO in advance of implementation.

C.12.2.1.15. MAINTENANCE. The Contractor shall ensure that the system, once operational, is properly maintained and monitored, to include immediate response to critical security patches, routine maintenance windows to allow for system updates, and compliance with a defined configuration management process. All patches and system updates shall be properly tested in a development environment before being implemented in the production environment. C.12.3. Adhere to Other Confidentiality and Security Provisions Data from other sources may be required to test or validate existing measures and tools. In such cases, the Contractor shall adhere to the policies, security protocols and requirements of the data proprietor. In some instances, the Contractor may be required to submit data use agreements, formal data requests and/or request Institutional Review Board approval for use of hospital specific records. C.12.4. Adhere to Legal Protections


The statute that governs AHRQ activities (Section 924[c] of the Public Health Service Act [42 U.S.C. 299c-3(c)]) (http://www.ahrq.gov/policymakers/hrqa99a.html), requires that information that might identify an individual cannot be used for any purpose other than the explicit purpose for which it is collected. In the case of the HCUP data, the purpose is limited to conducting research and developing statistical estimates. Information that could be used to identify persons, either those included in the database or those who are the source of information, cannot be released without specific permission from the individual. In addition to the statute that deals specifically with AHRQ, the Agency, like all Federal agencies, must adhere to the protections included in the Privacy Act of 1974 (as amended) (5 U.S.C. 552a) www.justice.gov/opcl/privstat.htm. This Act also restricts the use and dissemination of identifiable information and imposes criminal penalties for violations. The Privacy Act is similar to, but not as restrictive as, the specific AHRQ statutory protections.

AHRQ's use of the HCUP data acquired from the data organization is also subject to any other limitations that may be imposed on or by the data organization. Specifically, AHRQ shall observe and be bound by any state statutory requirements governing the data organization's release of these data and any additional requirements specified in the HCUP MOA and its addenda between AHRQ and the data organization. C.12.5. Catalogue and Return All Data All data files provided under this contract are for the sole purpose of supporting the AHRQ QI maintenance and update process and may not be used for any other purpose. Data files used under this contract shall be catalogued and returned to AHRQ at the completion of the task unless otherwise specified by the COR. Data shall be provided to the Contractor either on CD, DVD or via a secure Internet transfer to a central AHRQ data warehouse. It is possible that

future years of this contract shall require other formats and/or media based on emerging or existing technologies. C.12.6. Complete Privacy Training Tools on Security and Confidentiality of Data HCUP requires privacy training for all persons given access to HCUP data (both internal and external to AHRQ). AHRQ staff and contractors are required to sign an HCUP DUA, and Staff/Contractor Agreement. Electronic HCUP privacy training has been developed for internal AHRQ staff and Contractors and is required on an annual basis. The HCUP Privacy Training Tool and DUA Training Tool are maintained on the HCUP-US Web site (links will be provided by the government at the appropriate time). The Contractor shall keep a detailed log of all staff that have fulfilled the HHS and HCUP data security and privacy requirements and update on an annual basis. The Contractor should estimate this requiring approximately 90 minutes annually per project staff with access to data.

C.13. Support and Maintain Measures Based on Electronic Health Records Healthcare adoption and use of EHRs creates new opportunities for the AHRQ QI program. By utilizing this rich source of clinical information, the AHRQ QIs have the potential to identify potential quality concerns more quickly and more accurately than ever before. Electronic capture and real-time access to clinical patient data will likely facilitate communication of care between health care providers to ensure overall better quality of care. To this end, AHRQ is positioning its AHRQ QIs to be able to capitalize on the clinical data documented in EHRs such that any hospitals and/or systems that are transitioning to the electronic environment can generate them in a timely and accurate manner. The purpose of this task is to electronically specify existing AHRQ QIs that will be used for reporting by hospitals using certified EHR systems. As noted earlier, several AHRQ QIs are included in the CMS EHR incentive programs. The reporting of the electronic AHRQ QIs by hospitals to CMS must be in a standardized transmission format such as the Quality Reporting Document Architecture (QRDA) which will support the CMS electronic quality measure standard format used in the electronic specifications. To ensure consistency within HHS, AHRQ will be utilizing existing federal emeasure-related tools in this effort.

Page 71 of 174

Solicitation No. 14-233-SOL-00087 Support for AHRQ Quality Indicators IV

Beginning in Option Year 2, the Contractor shall: 1. Utilize the CMS measure authoring tool (MAT)), the CMS quality data model (QDM) and the CMS standardized repository for value sets (Value Set Authority Center ­ VSAC) when transitioning the AHRQ QIs to the EHR environment. 2. Ensure that the electronic QIs are consistent with industry standards for abstracting data from EHRs and transmitting data to CMS such as the Healthcare Quality Measurement Form (HQMF) and the Quality Reporting Document Architecture (QRDA). 3. Ensure that testing processes for measure e-specifications, including data elements, measure logic, shall occur throughout the transition process. 4. Ensure that the final e-specifications are ready for certification by the Office of the National Coordinator (ONC). This includes but is not limited to knowing industry standards and collaboration across federal agencies and with other stakeholders. 6. Serve as the subject matter expert on EHRs and respond to questions on the e-measures as needed. C.13.1: Evaluate existing eMeasure specifications The Contractor shall explore, evaluate, and incorporate existing methodologies developed for the creation of electronic specifications of quality measures, obtaining the input of experts in this field as necessary. C.13.2: Develop eSpecifications The Contractor shall develop electronic specifications for up to 15 existing AHRQ QIs as selected by AHRQ each year, and successfully test using a certified EHR. Include all applicable code sets based on standards issued by the Office of the National Coordinator. C.13.3: Develop and implement maintenance plan The Contractor shall develop and implement a maintenance plan for eMeasures created under this task. Maintenance and updates will include, but is not limited to, creating implementation test data files to enhance and/or improve the eMeasures, updating new codes/value sets, updating logic, and monitoring for continued NQF endorsement. C.13.4: Support eMeasure technical documents The Contractor shall develop all technical documents and guidance associated with the measures developed/electronically specified over the course of this contract, to be used as part of an education and outreach plan. This task also includes responding to and tracking eSpecification questions and issues raised by implementers, and providing Train-the-Trainer education and /or materials to a contract yet established to carry our Education and Outreach.

C.14. PREPARE AND SUBMIT AHRQ QIS TO THE NATIONAL QUALITY FORUM FOR ANNUAL UPDATES Below is an overview of the NQF endorsement and associated processes as it relates to NQF endorsed AHRQ QIs. The endorsement and maintenance process requires the demonstration that measures meet a certain standard, and the evaluation of the measures should be based on rigorous, current, evidence-based methodology as prescribed on the NQF endorsement process (www.qualityforum.org). NQF endorses measures only if they pass four measure evaluation criteria: Importance to Measure and Report, Scientific Acceptability of Measure Properties, Usability, and Feasibility. More detailed information as well as the measure submission process can be found at the NQF website: www.qualityforum.org/Measuring_Performance/Consensus_Development_Process.aspx For purposes of estimating resources and costs, the Contractor shall assume: 25 measures submitted for annual updates. See the following website for new measure submission: http://www.qualityforum.org/Measuring_Performance/Submitting_Standards.aspx . The Contractor shall designate one individual with experience with NQF submissions to coordinate the submission of annual update materials to NQF. This individual shall have experience and knowledge of clinical terminology. The Contractor shall maintain and regularly update a schedule of NQF submissions, including the history of endorsement of indicators, all submissions and all updates. The Contractor shall participate in monthly development calls, NQF annual meeting and ad-hoc meetings, as directed by the COR. C.14.1. Maintain NQF Endorsed AHRQ QI Measures In late 2010, the NQF maintenance process was revised to essentially mirror the initial measure submission process in terms of the type and extent of effort of the measure stewards. See the section above for details. Maintenance occurs every three years for each measure, but could be within 18 months of the previous endorsement depending on the dates of steering committee meetings. There are some variations in the maintenance process compared to the initial submission process. One difference is a comment phase regarding users' experiences with the implementation of the measure. All such comments on the AHRQ QIs require review and a typed response. Given that the NQF measure maintenance is on a 18-month to three-year cycle, and assuming the current NQF maintenance schedule, AHRQ anticipates that in a given year an average of 18 measures will be due for maintenance. The deadlines for submission of maintenance material are dependent on NQF schedules of Steering Committee meetings. The Contractor shall perform such activities as, but not limited to: a) Completion of measure submission form (assuming portions of the material in the pre-populated form are relevant and other aspects require revising) b) Preparation for, and participation in, three NQF committee meetings by 2 staff via conference call or webinar
Page 73 of 174

Solicitation No. 14-233-SOL-00087 Support for AHRQ Quality Indicators IV

c) Responding to comments in the review and comment phase and ad hoc follow up requests from the above steps The Contractor shall submit all completed forms for COR review and approval within 3 weeks of NQF submission deadline. Following approval, the Contractor shall submit all necessary documentation to NQF. C.14.2. Summary Report on NQF Activity The Contractor shall summarize all activities in Section C.14 in an annual report to the AHRQ COR.

C.15. Maintain Inventory of AHRQ QIs Used in Published Literature, Grey Literature and Public Reports The Contractor shall search for and maintain a list of organizations that use AHRQ QI measures in national, state or local public reporting or pay for performance programs, quality improvement efforts and public health initiatives. The Contractor shall also create and maintain a bibliography of published articles and an inventory of reports on the use of the AHRQ QIs for quality improvement, public reporting and pay for performance purposes. The Contractor shall employ a systematic approach to identifying these organizations and locating these publications and reports. Publications of interest include, but are not limited to, articles in peer-reviewed research and trade journals, professional forums, newspapers, and magazines. Reports of interest include, but are not limited to those published by Federal government agencies (e.g., GAO), state governments, healthcare organizations (e.g., Blue Cross), etc. The Contractor shall update the list and inventory every 12 months and shall include specifics on the organizational sponsor, specific AHRQ QI measures used in the initiative and any other relevant information.

The Contractor shall deliver software, documentation and web files deemed by the COR as the annual project files.

Each new module shall be released in a user-friendly manner with complete and helpful documentation, consistent with those for existing measures and tools. Prior to the release of all new tools/modules, the Contractor shall perform thorough double checks and tests of them, following the quality control process described in Section C.7. C.19. Redesign the AHRQ QI Windows Software Architecture (OPTION) Currently AHRQ maintains two platforms (SAS and Windows) which support the calculation of the AHRQ QI rates. This requires updates and testing in duplicate thereby increasing costs and probability for error. The Contractor shall evaluate the current design, capability and uses of the AHRQ QI software tools to determine alternative design options for the Windows-based software that would provide the AHRQ and the user community with the same capacity as SAS in an enhanced Windows platform that maximizes efficiency and minimizes error, resource burden and cost. C.19.1. Provide Recommendations for the Redesign of the QI Windows Software Architecture The Contractor shall develop a set of recommendations for the redesign of the AHRQ QI software architecture which achieve objectives including but not limited to:

-

Eliminate duplication of effort when updating or enhancing the SAS and Windows software tools Minimize chances of errors when updating, adding new capabilities, and testing the software Analyze large data sets more quickly and efficiently Calculate AHRQ QI rates more quickly Increase statistical capability (e.g. trend analyses) Increase efficiency when testing changes Facilitate modularity of the software so that new components can be added without impacting existing components Maintain transparency of the software code Increase usability of the measures and Windows software tools Increase functionality of the Windows software tools

-

Within 3 months of option award, the Contractor shall develop a report of this evaluation which describes various approaches to addressing the problem, their advantages and disadvantages and a final recommendation for restructuring and redesigning the AHRQ QI tools such that updates and maintenance activities can be done efficiently and expeditiously. C.21. Increase Use of AHRQ QIs and Demonstrate Impact (Option) Outreach efforts are needed to promote the use of AHRQ QI measures and tools and expand its value among current and potential users.
